  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d323d0f3-3800-4480-9e19-4364289d2d30'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer1158618658707534754">Emma Ross is a hard-working, quiet girl who tries to stay off the radar. It's all going okay for her until she starts getting along with one of the 'It' boys. Having this happen, comes with drama and pain, is it all worth it? Or it is just best to stay out of it all? As Emma battles with the conflict, which will she choose? It might just be the best thing for her...</span>

  <span id="freeText920220770441162150" style="display:none">So after a week or so, I'm ready to write my review. <br />If I had the option of zero stars, I would choose that one. <br />This are the types of books that should stay on wattpad. Drama!!!- everything and I mean, everything happened to the main character. From being in a car crash to being almost raped. From a mother that comes back from the dead to her BFF getting pregnant from her ( the main characters) brother. <br />If you wanted to put so many things- make it a series...idk. Or in second thought; don't. <br />OH! And let's not forget the annoying<br />Talking- <br />Person #1: he. Didn't. Kiss. Me<br />Person#2: yes. He. Did. <br />Person #1: no. He. Didn't. <br />I could understand of they say it once in awhile for emphasize, but not in every single chapter or in every single "major" plot line. <br />(I didn't write the characters names, cause I can't, for the life of me, remeber it. That's how forgettable they were)<br />Anyway, I jumped from one chapter to the other, skipped pages and just did everything to get to the end so I could say I finished it. And nothing major happened in the Pages I skipped. You could've easily understood the book if you read page number 1-30 and then 300-301 and so on. It was 500 and something pages for no apparent. Reason. (Isn't it annoying this type of writing?!) <br /><br />I don't recommend this book. At all ! <br />Save your money.</span>

<div id="review_1093557152" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1093557152" />
    <a title="Frances" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16528623-frances"><img alt="Frances" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586806935p2/16528623.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1093557152?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Frances" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Frances" href="/user/show/16528623-frances">Frances</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23396937-the-best-thing-for-me">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1093557152" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13191104104271169935">Another book that should have stayed on Wattpad as a free read, <u>because <b>AS IS</b></u>, it is not worth the money you spend to purchase.<br/><br/>This book has potential but it needs serious editing and reality check. The need for editing is not due to grammar errors, instead it's due at the choppy reading experience. You drastically jump from one scene to another and are left wondering if there are parts missing in the text due to a formatting error because you have <u><b>NO TRANSITION</b> what so ever</u> between scenes most </span>
  <span id="freeText13191104104271169935" style="display:none">Another book that should have stayed on Wattpad as a free read, <u>because <b>AS IS</b></u>, it is not worth the money you spend to purchase.<br /><br />This book has potential but it needs serious editing and reality check. The need for editing is not due to grammar errors, instead it's due at the choppy reading experience. You drastically jump from one scene to another and are left wondering if there are parts missing in the text due to a formatting error because you have <u><b>NO TRANSITION</b> what so ever</u> between scenes most of the time.<br /><br />But the biggest problem I found with this book was <i>the need for a reality check</i>, seriously!! Since the beginning I kept saying to myself, "keep reading, keep reading, it might just be an awkward start, but it'll smooth out and reality will set back in..." I got the the middle point at around 215pgs and just couldn't take it anymore when another ridiculous event showed up when the last one had just ended and I had thought "now we'll get to the good stuff." Emma, the heroine, just has one too many problems that should have involved the authorities since the beginning, but guess what, nobody, not even her "over protective" father ever once thought about contacting them. I mean, come on, that's just not even real!! Especially since she's just a teenager with no connections or special powers to save herself or do anything about it at all.<br /><br />Again, <b>AS IS</b>, I felt like I just wasted my time. BUT, and this is a big BUT, if the author spends some time on serious editing and twicking the storyline with some serious reality I think it could turn into a good book.<br /><br />Happy readings!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13191104104271169935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SObRUXzF1YG0uqvw0QTMeXuANbZ8vhjLKQ0qhIlV9mK7AY9AFyayZdE+52R5oxMaOKz4g27kOdPn46a/njyEqw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

Oh, how stupidly in love with that boy I was. He was the first boy that made me blush, my first official crush. Sounds beautiful so far, right? That excitement that bubbles up inside you, those famous butterflies you feel for the very first time—he was the reason for them all. But, you only get to live in that fairytale world until they crush your hopes and dreams and then stomp on your heart for good measure. And boy did he crush my little heart into pieces.  After the stomping part he became the boy I did my best to stay away from—and let me tell you, it was pretty hard to do when he slept in the room right across from mine. When tragedy struck his family and they moved away, I was ready to forget he ever existed.  Now he is a movie star, the one who makes women of all ages go into a screaming frenzy, the one who makes everyone swoon with that dimpled smile of his. Do you think that’s dreamy? I certainly don’t think so. How about me coming face to face with him? Nope still not dreamy. Not when I can’t even manage to look him in the eye.  Me? I’m Olive, a new writer.
